<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Additional_definitions_of_green">Additional definitions of green</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shades_of_green&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Additional definitions of green">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="Green_.28CMYK.29_.28pigment_green.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Green_(CMYK)_(pigment_green)">Green (CMYK) (pigment green)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shades_of_green&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Green (CMYK) (pigment green)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold">Green (CMYK) (pigment green)</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height:12px; background-color:#00A550; border: 0.1px solid #000000">
 </td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><span style="position: relative; float: right; font-size: 70%"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Color/Normalized_Color_Coordinates" title="About these coordinates"><img alt="About these coordinates" data-file-height="60" data-file-width="60" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/15px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/23px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/30px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 2x" width="15"/></a></span>     Color coordinates</th></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Web_colors#Hex_triplet" title="Web colors">Hex triplet</a></th><td>
#00A550</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SRGB_color_space" title="SRGB color space">sRGB</a><sup><b>B</b></sup>  (<a href="/wiki/Red" title="Red">r</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green" title="Green">g</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blue" title="Blue">b</a>)</th><td>
(00, 165, 80)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/CMYK_color_model" title="CMYK color model">CMYK</a><sup><b>H</b></sup>   (<a href="/wiki/Cyan" title="Cyan">c</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magenta" title="Magenta">m</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yellow" title="Yellow">y</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black" title="Black">k</a>)</span></th><td>
<span class="nowrap">(100, 0, 100, 0)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><span class="nowrap"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HSV_color_space" title="HSV color space">HSV</a>       (<a href="/wiki/Hue" title="Hue">h</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saturation_(color_theory)" title="Saturation (color theory)">s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brightness" title="Brightness">v</a>)</span></th><td>
<span class="nowrap">(149°, 100%, 65%)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Source</th><td>
<a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20070310213952/http://www.tintbook.com/" rel="nofollow">CMYK</a></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<b>B</b>: Normalized to [0–255] (byte)<br/><b>H</b>: Normalized to [0–100] (hundred)</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SubtractiveColor.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="400" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/SubtractiveColor.svg/140px-SubtractiveColor.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/SubtractiveColor.svg/210px-SubtractiveColor.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/SubtractiveColor.svg/280px-SubtractiveColor.svg.png 2x" width="140"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SubtractiveColor.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Cyan" title="Cyan">Cyan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magenta" title="Magenta">magenta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yellow" title="Yellow">yellow</a> are the three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subtractive_primary" title="Subtractive primary">subtractive primary</a> colors used in <a href="/wiki/Printing" title="Printing">printing</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The color defined as <i>green</i> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CMYK" title="CMYK">CMYK</a> color system used in <a href="/wiki/Printing" title="Printing">printing</a>, also known as <i>pigment green</i>, is the tone of green that is achieved by mixing process (printer's) cyan and process (printer's) yellow in equal proportions. It is displayed at right.
</p><p>The purpose of the CMYK color system is to provide the maximum possible gamut of color reproducible in printing.
</p><p>The color indicated is only approximate as the colors of printing inks may vary.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span id="Green_.28NCS.29_.28psychological_primary_green.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Green_(NCS)_(psychological_primary_green)">Green (NCS) (psychological primary green)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shades_of_green&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Green (NCS) (psychological primary green)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold">Green (NCS)</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height:12px; background-color:#009F6B; border: 0.1px solid #000000">
 </td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><span style="position: relative; float: right; font-size: 70%"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Color/Normalized_Color_Coordinates" title="About these coordinates"><img alt="About these coordinates" data-file-height="60" data-file-width="60" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/15px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/23px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/30px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 2x" width="15"/></a></span>     Color coordinates</th></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Web_colors#Hex_triplet" title="Web colors">Hex triplet</a></th><td>
#009F6B</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SRGB_color_space" title="SRGB color space">sRGB</a><sup><b>B</b></sup>  (<a href="/wiki/Red" title="Red">r</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green" title="Green">g</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blue" title="Blue">b</a>)</th><td>
(0, 159, 107)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><span class="nowrap"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HSV_color_space" title="HSV color space">HSV</a>       (<a href="/wiki/Hue" title="Hue">h</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saturation_(color_theory)" title="Saturation (color theory)">s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brightness" title="Brightness">v</a>)</span></th><td>
<span class="nowrap">(160°, 100%, 63%)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Source</th><td>
sRGB approximation to <span class="nowrap">NCS 2060-G</span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<b>B</b>: Normalized to [0–255] (byte)<br/></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Opponent_colors.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="743" data-file-width="1050" height="99" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Opponent_colors.svg/140px-Opponent_colors.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Opponent_colors.svg/210px-Opponent_colors.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Opponent_colors.svg/280px-Opponent_colors.svg.png 2x" width="140"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Opponent_colors.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Approximations within the sRGB gamut to the primary colors of the <a href="/wiki/Natural_Color_System" title="Natural Color System">Natural Color System</a>, a model based on the <a href="/wiki/Opponent_process" title="Opponent process">opponent process</a> theory of color vision.</div></div></div>
<p>The color defined as <i>green</i> in the NCS or <a href="/wiki/Natural_Color_System" title="Natural Color System">Natural Color System</a> is shown at right (NCS 2060-G). The natural color system is a color system based on the four <a href="/wiki/Unique_hues" title="Unique hues">unique hues</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Psychological_primary_color" title="Psychological primary color">psychological primary colors</a> red, yellow, green, and blue. The NCS is based on the <a href="/wiki/Opponent_process" title="Opponent process">opponent process</a> theory of vision.
</p><p>The Natural Color System is widely used in <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavia</a>.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span id="Green_.28Munsell.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Green_(Munsell)">Green (Munsell)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shades_of_green&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Green (Munsell)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold">Green (Munsell)</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height:12px; background-color:#00A877; border: 0.1px solid #000000">
 </td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><span style="position: relative; float: right; font-size: 70%"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Color/Normalized_Color_Coordinates" title="About these coordinates"><img alt="About these coordinates" data-file-height="60" data-file-width="60" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/15px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/23px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/30px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 2x" width="15"/></a></span>     Color coordinates</th></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Web_colors#Hex_triplet" title="Web colors">Hex triplet</a></th><td>
#00A877</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SRGB_color_space" title="SRGB color space">sRGB</a><sup><b>B</b></sup>  (<a href="/wiki/Red" title="Red">r</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green" title="Green">g</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blue" title="Blue">b</a>)</th><td>
(0, 168, 119)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/CMYK_color_model" title="CMYK color model">CMYK</a><sup><b>H</b></sup>   (<a href="/wiki/Cyan" title="Cyan">c</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magenta" title="Magenta">m</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yellow" title="Yellow">y</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black" title="Black">k</a>)</span></th><td>
<span class="nowrap">(100, 0, 29, 54)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><span class="nowrap"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HSV_color_space" title="HSV color space">HSV</a>       (<a href="/wiki/Hue" title="Hue">h</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saturation_(color_theory)" title="Saturation (color theory)">s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brightness" title="Brightness">v</a>)</span></th><td>
<span class="nowrap">(163°, 100%, 66%)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Source</th><td>
<a href="/wiki/File:MunsellColorWheel.svg" title="File:MunsellColorWheel.svg">Munsell Color Wheel</a></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<b>B</b>: Normalized to [0–255] (byte)<br/><b>H</b>: Normalized to [0–100] (hundred)</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MunsellColorWheel.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="550" data-file-width="550" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/MunsellColorWheel.svg/140px-MunsellColorWheel.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/MunsellColorWheel.svg/210px-MunsellColorWheel.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/MunsellColorWheel.svg/280px-MunsellColorWheel.svg.png 2x" width="140"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MunsellColorWheel.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The hues of the <a href="/wiki/Munsell_color_system" title="Munsell color system">Munsell color system</a>, at varying values, and maximum chroma to stay in the sRGB gamut.</div></div></div>
<p>The color defined as <i>green</i> in the <a href="/wiki/Munsell_color_system" title="Munsell color system">Munsell color system</a> (Munsell 5G) is shown at right. The Munsell color system is a <a href="/wiki/Color_space" title="Color space">color space</a> that specifies colors based on three color dimensions: hue, value (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lightness_(color)" title="Lightness (color)">lightness</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Colorfulness" title="Colorfulness">chroma</a> (color purity), spaced uniformly in three dimensions in the elongated oval at an angle shaped Munsell <a href="/wiki/Color_solid" title="Color solid">color solid</a> according to the <a href="/wiki/Logarithmic_scale" title="Logarithmic scale">logarithmic scale</a> which governs <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_perception" title="Human perception">human perception</a>. In order for all the colors to be spaced uniformly, it was found necessary to use a color wheel with five primary colors—red, yellow, green, blue and purple.
</p><p>The Munsell colors displayed are only approximate as they have been adjusted to fit into the sRGB gamut.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span id="Green_.28Pantone.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Green_(Pantone)">Green (Pantone)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shades_of_green&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Green (Pantone)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold">Green (Pantone)</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height:12px; background-color:#00AD83; border: 0.1px solid #000000">
 </td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><span style="position: relative; float: right; font-size: 70%"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Color/Normalized_Color_Coordinates" title="About these coordinates"><img alt="About these coordinates" data-file-height="60" data-file-width="60" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/15px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/23px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/30px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 2x" width="15"/></a></span>     Color coordinates</th></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Web_colors#Hex_triplet" title="Web colors">Hex triplet</a></th><td>
#00AD83</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SRGB_color_space" title="SRGB color space">sRGB</a><sup><b>B</b></sup>  (<a href="/wiki/Red" title="Red">r</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green" title="Green">g</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blue" title="Blue">b</a>)</th><td>
(0, 173, 131)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/CMYK_color_model" title="CMYK color model">CMYK</a><sup><b>H</b></sup>   (<a href="/wiki/Cyan" title="Cyan">c</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magenta" title="Magenta">m</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yellow" title="Yellow">y</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black" title="Black">k</a>)</span></th><td>
<span class="nowrap">(100, 0, 24, 32)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><span class="nowrap"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HSV_color_space" title="HSV color space">HSV</a>       (<a href="/wiki/Hue" title="Hue">h</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saturation_(color_theory)" title="Saturation (color theory)">s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brightness" title="Brightness">v</a>)</span></th><td>
<span class="nowrap">(165°, 100%, 68%)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Source</th><td>
<a class="external text" href="http://www.pantone.com/pages/pantone/colorfinder.aspx" rel="nofollow">Pantone TPX</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<b>B</b>: Normalized to [0–255] (byte)<br/><b>H</b>: Normalized to [0–100] (hundred)</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><i>Green (Pantone)</i> is the color that is called <i>green</i> in <a href="/wiki/Pantone" title="Pantone">Pantone</a>.
</p><p>The source of this color is the "<a href="/wiki/Pantone" title="Pantone">Pantone</a> Textile Paper eXtended (TPX)" color list, color # green C, EC, HC, PC, U, or UP—green.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span id="Green_.28Crayola.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Green_(Crayola)">Green (Crayola)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shades_of_green&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Green (Crayola)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold">Green (Crayola)</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height:12px; background-color:#1CAC78; border: 0.1px solid #000000">

<span class="nowrap">(158°, 84%, 68%)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Source</th><td>

<b>B</b>: Normalized to [0–255] (byte)<br/><b>H</b>: Normalized to [0–100] (hundred)</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><i>Green (Crayola)</i> is the color called <i>green</i> in Crayola crayons.
</p><p>Green was one of the original Crayola crayons introduced in 1903.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Army_green">Army green</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shades_of_green&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Army green">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold">Army green</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height:12px; background-color:#4B5320; border: 0.1px solid #000000">

<p>The color <i>army green</i> has been used in militaries since at least World War II, and possibly before, though the precise tint varies considerably between and within different nations. (See <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olive_drab" title="Olive drab">olive drab</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olive_green" title="Olive green">olive green</a>)
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bottle_green">Bottle green</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shades_of_green&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Bottle green">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold">Bottle green</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height:12px; background-color:#006A4E; border: 0.1px solid #000000">
 </td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><span style="position: relative; float: right; font-size: 70%"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Color/Normalized_Color_Coordinates" title="About these coordinates"><img alt="About these coordinates" data-file-height="60" data-file-width="60" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/15px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/23px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/30px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 2x" width="15"/></a></span>     Color coordinates</th></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Web_colors#Hex_triplet" title="Web colors">Hex triplet</a></th><td>
#006A4E</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SRGB_color_space" title="SRGB color space">sRGB</a><sup><b>B</b></sup>  (<a href="/wiki/Red" title="Red">r</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green" title="Green">g</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blue" title="Blue">b</a>)</th><td>
(0, 106, 78)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/CMYK_color_model" title="CMYK color model">CMYK</a><sup><b>H</b></sup>   (<a href="/wiki/Cyan" title="Cyan">c</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magenta" title="Magenta">m</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yellow" title="Yellow">y</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black" title="Black">k</a>)</span></th><td>
<span class="nowrap">(100, 0, 26, 58<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ency_006A4E_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ency_006A4E-41">[41]</a></sup>)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><span class="nowrap"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HSV_color_space" title="HSV color space">HSV</a>       (<a href="/wiki/Hue" title="Hue">h</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saturation_(color_theory)" title="Saturation (color theory)">s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brightness" title="Brightness">v</a>)</span></th><td>
<span class="nowrap">(164°, 100%, 42<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ency_006A4E_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ency_006A4E-41">[41]</a></sup>%)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Source</th><td>
<a class="external text" href="http://encycolorpedia.com/006a4e" rel="nofollow">Encycolorpedia</a></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<b>B</b>: Normalized to [0–255] (byte)<br/><b>H</b>: Normalized to [0–100] (hundred)</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><i>Bottle green</i> is a dark shade of green, similar to pine green. It is a representation of the color of green <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glass_bottles" title="Glass bottles">glass bottles</a>.
</p><p>The first recorded use of <i>bottle green</i> as a color name in English was in 1816.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Bottle green</i> is a color in <a href="/wiki/Prismacolor" title="Prismacolor">Prismacolor</a> marker and pencil sets. It is also the color of the uniform of the <a href="/wiki/Police_Service_of_Northern_Ireland" title="Police Service of Northern Ireland">Police Service of Northern Ireland</a> replacing the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Ulster_Constabulary" title="Royal Ulster Constabulary">Royal Ulster Constabulary</a>'s "rifle green" colored uniforms in 2001. It also the green used in uniforms for <a href="/wiki/South_Sydney_High_School" title="South Sydney High School">South Sydney High School</a> in Sydney.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Bottle green</i> is also the color most associated with guide signs and street name signs in the United States.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:D%C3%BClmen,_Alte_Brennerei_L%C3%B6hning_--_2015_--_8677-81.jpg"><img alt="Green bottles on a windowsill" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3431" data-file-width="5139" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/D%C3%BClmen%2C_Alte_Brennerei_L%C3%B6hning_--_2015_--_8677-81.jpg/220px-D%C3%BClmen%2C_Alte_Brennerei_L%C3%B6hning_--_2015_--_8677-81.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/D%C3%BClmen%2C_Alte_Brennerei_L%C3%B6hning_--_2015_--_8677-81.jpg/330px-D%C3%BClmen%2C_Alte_Brennerei_L%C3%B6hning_--_2015_--_8677-81.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/D%C3%BClmen%2C_Alte_Brennerei_L%C3%B6hning_--_2015_--_8677-81.jpg/440px-D%C3%BClmen%2C_Alte_Brennerei_L%C3%B6hning_--_2015_--_8677-81.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:D%C3%BClmen,_Alte_Brennerei_L%C3%B6hning_--_2015_--_8677-81.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Green bottles on a windowsill</div></div></div>
<p>Bottle green is also the background color of the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Bangladesh" title="Flag of Bangladesh">Flag of Bangladesh</a>, as defined by the government of Bangladesh.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flagrule_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-flagrule-44">[44]</a></sup> Another name for this color is <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bangladesh_green" title="Bangladesh green">Bangladesh green</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template"><span style="white-space: nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Link_rot" title="Wikipedia:Link rot"><span title=" Dead link since September 2018">dead link</span></a></i>]</span></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bright_green">Bright green</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shades_of_green&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Bright green">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold">Bright green</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height:12px; background-color:#66FF00; border: 0.1px solid #000000">
 </td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><span style="position: relative; float: right; font-size: 70%"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Color/Normalized_Color_Coordinates" title="About these coordinates"><img alt="About these coordinates" data-file-height="60" data-file-width="60" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/15px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/23px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/30px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 2x" width="15"/></a></span>     Color coordinates</th></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Web_colors#Hex_triplet" title="Web colors">Hex triplet</a></th><td>
#66FF00</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SRGB_color_space" title="SRGB color space">sRGB</a><sup><b>B</b></sup>  (<a href="/wiki/Red" title="Red">r</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green" title="Green">g</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blue" title="Blue">b</a>)</th><td>
(102, 255, 0)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/CMYK_color_model" title="CMYK color model">CMYK</a><sup><b>H</b></sup>   (<a href="/wiki/Cyan" title="Cyan">c</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magenta" title="Magenta">m</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yellow" title="Yellow">y</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black" title="Black">k</a>)</span></th><td>
<span class="nowrap">(60, 0, 100, 0)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><span class="nowrap"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HSV_color_space" title="HSV color space">HSV</a>       (<a href="/wiki/Hue" title="Hue">h</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saturation_(color_theory)" title="Saturation (color theory)">s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brightness" title="Brightness">v</a>)</span></th><td>
<span class="nowrap">(96°, 100%, 100%)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Source</th><td>
<a class="external text" href="http://www.webdiner.com/annexe/hexcode/hexcode.htm" rel="nofollow">Hexcode Color Chart</a></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<b>B</b>: Normalized to [0–255] (byte)<br/><b>H</b>: Normalized to [0–100] (hundred)</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Displayed on the right is the color <i>bright green</i>. Bright green is a bright shade of green. It is on the color wheel approximately one-third of the way between <a href="/wiki/Chartreuse_(color)" title="Chartreuse (color)">chartreuse green</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harlequin_(color)" title="Harlequin (color)">harlequin (color #3FFF00)</a> (closer to chartreuse green than to harlequin). Bright green represents a visual stimulus of 556 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanometer" title="Nanometer">nanometers</a> on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Visual_spectrum" title="Visual spectrum">visual spectrum</a> as measured on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CIE_chromaticity_diagram" title="CIE chromaticity diagram">CIE chromaticity diagram</a>. The X11 color <i>green</i> is somewhat similar to bright green, with a hex triplet of #00FF00, compared to bright green's triplet of #66FF00.
</p><p>The color bright green is used to represent <a href="/wiki/Bright_green_environmentalism" title="Bright green environmentalism">bright green environmentalism</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> or the <a href="/wiki/Viridian_design_movement" title="Viridian design movement">Viridian design movement</a>.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<span class="nowrap">(65, 0, 20, 70)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><span class="nowrap"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HSV_color_space" title="HSV color space">HSV</a>       (<a href="/wiki/Hue" title="Hue">h</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saturation_(color_theory)" title="Saturation (color theory)">s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brightness" title="Brightness">v</a>)</span></th><td>
<span class="nowrap">(162°, 65%, 30%)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Source</th><td>
<sup>[<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Color/Sources_for_Color_Coordinates" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Color/Sources for Color Coordinates">Unsourced</a>]</sup></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<b>B</b>: Normalized to [0–255] (byte)<br/><b>H</b>: Normalized to [0–100] (hundred)</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><i>Brunswick green</i> is a common name for green pigments made from <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a> compounds, although the name has also been used for other formulations that produce a similar hue, such as mixtures of <a href="/wiki/Chrome_yellow" title="Chrome yellow">chrome yellow</a> and Prussian blue. The pigment is named after <a href="/wiki/Braunschweig" title="Braunschweig">Braunschweig</a>, Germany (also known as Brunswick in English) where it was first manufactured. It is a deep, dark green, which may vary from intense to very dark, almost black.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup>
</p><p>The first recorded use of <i>Brunswick green</i> as a color name in English was in 1764.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Another name for this color is <i>English green</i>. The first use of English green as a synonym for Brunswick green was in 1923.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Deep Brunswick green</i> is commonly recognized as part of the <a href="/wiki/British_racing_green" title="British racing green">British racing green</a> spectrum, the national <a href="/wiki/Auto_racing" title="Auto racing">auto racing</a> color of the United Kingdom.
</p><p>A different color, also called <i>Brunswick green</i>, was the color for passenger locomotives of the grouping and then the nationalized <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Railways" title="British Railways">British Railways</a>. There were three shades of these colors and they are defined under British Standard BS381C – 225, BS381C – 226, and BS381C – 227 (ordered from lightest to darkest). The Brunswick green used by the Nationalised British Railways – Western Region for passenger locomotives was BS381C – 227 (rgb(30:62:46)). RAL6005 is a close substitute to BS381C – 227. A characteristic of these colors was the ease for various railway locations to mix them by using whole pots of primary colors – hence the ability to get reasonably consistent colors with manual mixing half a century and more ago.
</p><p>The color used by the <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Railroad" title="Pennsylvania Railroad">Pennsylvania Railroad</a> for locomotives was often called <i>Brunswick green</i>, but officially was termed <i>dark green locomotive enamel</i> (DGLE). This was a shade of green so dark as to be almost black, but which turned greener with age and weathering as the copper compounds further oxidized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cal_Poly_Pomona_green">Cal Poly Pomona green</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shades_of_green&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Cal Poly Pomona green">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold">Cal Poly Pomona green</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height:12px; background-color:#1E4D2B; border: 0.1px solid #000000">

<b>B</b>: Normalized to [0–255] (byte)<br/><b>H</b>: Normalized to [0–100] (hundred)</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><i>Cal Poly Pomona green</i> is one of the two official colors of <a href="/wiki/California_State_Polytechnic_University,_Pomona" title="California State Polytechnic University, Pomona">California State Polytechnic University, Pomona</a> (Cal Poly Pomona). The official university colors are green (PMS 349) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cal_Poly_Pomona_gold" title="Cal Poly Pomona gold">gold (PMS 131)</a>. The Cal Poly Pomona Office of Public Affairs created the Cal Poly Pomona colors for web development and has technical guidelines, copyright and privacy protection; as well as logos and images that developers are asked to follow in the university's guidelines for using official Cal Poly Pomona logos. If web developers are using green on a university website, they are encouraged to use Cal Poly Pomona green. It is prominently used for representing Cal Poly Pomona's athletic teams, the <a href="/wiki/Cal_Poly_Pomona_Broncos" title="Cal Poly Pomona Broncos">Cal Poly Pomona Broncos</a>.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<p><i>Castleton green</i> is one of the two official colors of <a href="/wiki/Castleton_University" title="Castleton University">Castleton University</a> in Vermont. The official college colors are green (PMS 343) and white. The Castleton University Office of Marketing and Communications created the Castleton colors for web and logo development and has technical guidelines, copyright and privacy protection; as well as logos and images that developers are asked to follow in the college's guidelines for using official Castleton logos. If web developers are using green on a university website, they are encouraged to use Castleton green. It is prominently used for representing Castleton's athletic teams, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Castleton_Spartans" title="Castleton Spartans">Castleton Spartans</a>.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Celadon">Celadon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shades_of_green&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Celadon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold">Celadon</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height:12px; background-color:#ACE1AF; border: 0.1px solid #000000">
 </td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><span style="position: relative; float: right; font-size: 70%"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Color/Normalized_Color_Coordinates" title="About these coordinates"><img alt="About these coordinates" data-file-height="60" data-file-width="60" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/15px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/23px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/30px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 2x" width="15"/></a></span>     Color coordinates</th></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Web_colors#Hex_triplet" title="Web colors">Hex triplet</a></th><td>
#ACE1AF</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SRGB_color_space" title="SRGB color space">sRGB</a><sup><b>B</b></sup>  (<a href="/wiki/Red" title="Red">r</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green" title="Green">g</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blue" title="Blue">b</a>)</th><td>
(172, 225, 175)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/CMYK_color_model" title="CMYK color model">CMYK</a><sup><b>H</b></sup>   (<a href="/wiki/Cyan" title="Cyan">c</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magenta" title="Magenta">m</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yellow" title="Yellow">y</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black" title="Black">k</a>)</span></th><td>
<span class="nowrap">(24, 0, 22, 12)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><span class="nowrap"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HSV_color_space" title="HSV color space">HSV</a>       (<a href="/wiki/Hue" title="Hue">h</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saturation_(color_theory)" title="Saturation (color theory)">s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brightness" title="Brightness">v</a>)</span></th><td>
<span class="nowrap">(123°, 24%, 88%)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Source</th><td>
<a class="external text" href="http://encycolorpedia.com/ace1af" rel="nofollow">Encycolorpedia</a></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<b>B</b>: Normalized to [0–255] (byte)<br/><b>H</b>: Normalized to [0–100] (hundred)</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><i>Celadon</i> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">ɛ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span> is a pale greyish shade of green.
</p><p>According to dictionary.com, this pale green color can be traced to French literature of the 17th century. <i>Celadon</i> was the name of a character who wore green clothes in Honoré d'Urfé's novel <i>L’Astree</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Goryeo_Celadon.jpg"><img alt="A celadon vase" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="591" data-file-width="457" height="285" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Goryeo_Celadon.jpg/220px-Goryeo_Celadon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Goryeo_Celadon.jpg/330px-Goryeo_Celadon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Goryeo_Celadon.jpg/440px-Goryeo_Celadon.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Goryeo_Celadon.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Celadon" title="Celadon">celadon</a> vase</div></div></div>
<p>A glaze of this color is commonly used in Chinese and Korean pottery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> It is normally associated with a pale sea-green pigment though the style originally was made with much darker pigments. The pale green pigment came from the artisans who used specific clays and potting techniques to create the style now associated with the name. It was most commonly used in Chinese, Korean and Japanese art and spread to the other Asian cultures. Celadon, as it is known by the west, or <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Qingci&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Qingci (page does not exist)">qingci</a></i>, is an ancient type of Chinese <a href="/wiki/Glaze_(painting_technique)" title="Glaze (painting technique)">glaze</a> that was particularly favored at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Song_Dynasty" title="Song Dynasty">Song court</a>. These pots have blue-green glazes and are made in elegant shapes and were produced in <a href="/wiki/Kiln" title="Kiln">kilns</a> from all over China. <a href="/wiki/Korean_pottery_and_porcelain" title="Korean pottery and porcelain">Korean celadon pottery</a> has been described by ancient Chinese artisans as having a quiet elegance whose color is "beyond description", in that it must be experienced to be understood, and its simplicity of form and style has been compared to the spirit of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zen_Buddhism" title="Zen Buddhism">Zen Buddhism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dark_pastel_green">Dark pastel green</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shades_of_green&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Dark pastel green">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dartmouth_green">Dartmouth green</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shades_of_green&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Dartmouth green">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold">Dartmouth green</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height:12px; background-color:#00693E; border: 0.1px solid #000000">

<b>B</b>: Normalized to [0–255] (byte)<br/><b>H</b>: Normalized to [0–100] (hundred)</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><i>Dartmouth green</i> is the official color of <a href="/wiki/Dartmouth_College" title="Dartmouth College">Dartmouth College</a>, adopted in 1866. It was famously chosen after a crew race with a number of other colleges for being "the only decent color that had not been taken already".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> It is prominently used as the name of the Dartmouth College athletic team, the <a href="/wiki/Dartmouth_Big_Green" title="Dartmouth Big Green">Dartmouth Big Green</a>. The Dartmouth athletic teams adopted this new name after the college officially discontinued the use of its unofficial mascot, the Dartmouth Indian, in 1974.
</p><p>Dartmouth green and white are the main colors of Lithuanian basketball club <a href="/wiki/BC_%C5%BDalgiris" title="BC Žalgiris">Žalgiris Kaunas</a>.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Emerald">Emerald</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shades_of_green&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Emerald">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gachala_Emerald_3526711557_849c4c7367.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1698" data-file-width="2264" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Gachala_Emerald_3526711557_849c4c7367.jpg/170px-Gachala_Emerald_3526711557_849c4c7367.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Gachala_Emerald_3526711557_849c4c7367.jpg/255px-Gachala_Emerald_3526711557_849c4c7367.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Gachala_Emerald_3526711557_849c4c7367.jpg/340px-Gachala_Emerald_3526711557_849c4c7367.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gachala_Emerald_3526711557_849c4c7367.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Emerald" title="Emerald">emerald</a></div></div></div>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold">Emerald</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height:12px; background-color:#50C878; border: 0.1px solid #000000">
 </td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><span style="position: relative; float: right; font-size: 70%"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Color/Normalized_Color_Coordinates" title="About these coordinates"><img alt="About these coordinates" data-file-height="60" data-file-width="60" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/15px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/23px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/30px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 2x" width="15"/></a></span>     Color coordinates</th></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Web_colors#Hex_triplet" title="Web colors">Hex triplet</a></th><td>

<b>B</b>: Normalized to [0–255] (byte)<br/><b>H</b>: Normalized to [0–100] (hundred)</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><i>Emerald</i>, also called <i>emerald green</i>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> is a tone of green that is particularly light and bright, with a faint bluish cast. The name derives from the typical appearance of the gemstone <a href="/wiki/Emerald" title="Emerald">emerald</a>.
</p><p>The first recorded use of <i>emerald</i> as a color name in English was in 1598.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup>
</p><p>Ireland is sometimes referred to as the <i>Emerald Isle</i> due to its lush greenery. The May birthstone is emerald. Seattle is sometimes referred to as the <i>Emerald City</i>, because its abundant rainfall creates lush vegetation. In the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, <i>The <a href="/wiki/Emerald_Tablet" title="Emerald Tablet">Emerald Tablet</a> of <a href="/wiki/Hermes_Trismegistus" title="Hermes Trismegistus">Hermes Trismegistus</a></i> was believed to contain the secrets of <a href="/wiki/Alchemy" title="Alchemy">alchemy</a>. "Emerald City", from the  story of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wonderful_Wizard_of_Oz" title="The Wonderful Wizard of Oz">The Wonderful Wizard of Oz</a></i>, by L. Frank Baum, is a city where everything from food to people are emerald green. However, it is revealed at the end of the story that everything in the city is normal colored, but the glasses everyone wears are emerald tinted. The <a href="/wiki/Green_Zone" title="Green Zone">Green Zone</a> in Baghdad is sometimes ironically and cynically referred to as the <i>Emerald City</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Emerald_Buddha" title="Emerald Buddha">Emerald Buddha</a></i> is a figurine of the sitting Buddha, made of green <a href="/wiki/Jade" title="Jade">jade</a> (rather than emerald), clothed in gold, and about 45 cm tall. It is kept in the <i>Chapel of the Emerald Buddha</i> (<a href="/wiki/Wat_Phra_Kaew" title="Wat Phra Kaew">Wat Phra Kaew</a>) on the grounds of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Palace,_Bangkok" title="Grand Palace, Bangkok">Grand Palace</a> in Bangkok. The <a href="/wiki/Emerald_Triangle" title="Emerald Triangle">Emerald Triangle</a> refers to the three counties of <a href="/wiki/Mendocino_County,_California" title="Mendocino County, California">Mendocino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Humboldt_County,_California" title="Humboldt County, California">Humboldt</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Trinity_County,_California" title="Trinity County, California">Trinity</a> in Northern California, United States<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Regan_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-Regan-58">[58]</a></sup>
because these three counties are the biggest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marijuana" title="Marijuana">marijuana</a> producing counties in California and also the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Regan_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-Regan-58">[58]</a></sup> A county-commissioned study reports pot accounts for up to two-thirds of the economy of Mendocino.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Regan_58-2"><a href="#cite_note-Regan-58">[58]</a></sup> <i>Emerald Cities: Urban Sustainability and Economic Development</i> is a book published in 2010 by Joan Fitzgerald, director of the law, policy and society program at <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_University" title="Northeastern University">Northeastern University</a>, about <a href="/wiki/Ecodesign" title="Ecodesign">ecologically sustainable</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/City_planning" title="City planning">city planning</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rough_emerald_crystals_from_Panjshir_Valley_Afghanistan.jpg"><img alt="Emerald crystals" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1688" data-file-width="3008" height="123" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Rough_emerald_crystals_from_Panjshir_Valley_Afghanistan.jpg/220px-Rough_emerald_crystals_from_Panjshir_Valley_Afghanistan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Rough_emerald_crystals_from_Panjshir_Valley_Afghanistan.jpg/330px-Rough_emerald_crystals_from_Panjshir_Valley_Afghanistan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Rough_emerald_crystals_from_Panjshir_Valley_Afghanistan.jpg/440px-Rough_emerald_crystals_from_Panjshir_Valley_Afghanistan.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rough_emerald_crystals_from_Panjshir_Valley_Afghanistan.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Emerald" title="Emerald">Emerald</a> crystals</div></div></div>
<p>During the 19th century, the arsenic-containing dye <a href="/wiki/Paris_green" title="Paris green">Paris green</a> was marketed as emerald green.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Feldgrau">Feldgrau</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shades_of_green&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Feldgrau">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Feldgrau" title="Feldgrau">Feldgrau</a></div>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold">Feldgrau</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height:12px; background-color:#4D5D53; border: 0.1px solid #000000">
 </td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><span style="position: relative; float: right; font-size: 70%"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Color/Normalized_Color_Coordinates" title="About these coordinates"><img alt="About these coordinates" data-file-height="60" data-file-width="60" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/15px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/23px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/30px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 2x" width="15"/></a></span>     Color coordinates</th></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Web_colors#Hex_triplet" title="Web colors">Hex triplet</a></th><td>

(77, 93, 83)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><span class="nowrap"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HSV_color_space" title="HSV color space">HSV</a>       (<a href="/wiki/Hue" title="Hue">h</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saturation_(color_theory)" title="Saturation (color theory)">s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brightness" title="Brightness">v</a>)</span></th><td>

<b>B</b>: Normalized to [0–255] (byte)<br/></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><i>Feldgrau</i> (field grey) was the color of the field uniform of the <a href="/wiki/German_Army_(Wehrmacht)" title="German Army (Wehrmacht)">German Army</a> from late 1907 until 1945,  and the East German <a href="/wiki/National_People%27s_Army" title="National People's Army">NVA</a> armies. Metaphorically, <i>feldgrau</i> used to refer to the armies of Germany (the <a href="/wiki/German_Army_(German_Empire)" title="German Army (German Empire)">Imperial German Army</a> and the Heer [army] component of the <i>Reichswehr</i> and the <i>Wehrmacht</i>).
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="GO_Transit_green">GO Transit green</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shades_of_green&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: GO Transit green">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold">GO green</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height:12px; background-color:#00AB66; border: 0.1px solid #000000">
 </td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><span style="position: relative; float: right; font-size: 70%"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Color/Normalized_Color_Coordinates" title="About these coordinates"><img alt="About these coordinates" data-file-height="60" data-file-width="60" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/15px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/23px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/30px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 2x" width="15"/></a></span>     Color coordinates</th></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Web_colors#Hex_triplet" title="Web colors">Hex triplet</a></th><td>

<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lakeshore_West_GO_Train_Westbound.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1652" data-file-width="2064" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Lakeshore_West_GO_Train_Westbound.jpg/200px-Lakeshore_West_GO_Train_Westbound.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Lakeshore_West_GO_Train_Westbound.jpg/300px-Lakeshore_West_GO_Train_Westbound.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Lakeshore_West_GO_Train_Westbound.jpg/400px-Lakeshore_West_GO_Train_Westbound.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lakeshore_West_GO_Train_Westbound.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A GO Transit train on the <a href="/wiki/Lakeshore_West_line" title="Lakeshore West line">Lakeshore West line</a> in Toronto, Canada</div></div></div>
<p><i>GO green</i> was the color used for the brand of <a href="/wiki/GO_Transit" title="GO Transit">GO Transit</a>, the regional commuter service in the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Toronto_Area" title="Greater Toronto Area">Greater Toronto Area</a>. Between 1967 and 2013, the brand and color that has adorned each of its <a href="/wiki/Train" title="Train">train</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buses" title="Buses">buses</a>, and other property generally remained unchanged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> It also matched the shade of green used on signs for highways in Ontario. In July 2013, GO Transit updated its look to a two-tone color scheme.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<span class="nowrap">(84°, 82%, 100%)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Source</th><td>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_HTML_color_names" title="List of HTML color names">X11</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-css3-color_1-7"><a href="#cite_note-css3-color-1">[1]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<b>B</b>: Normalized to [0–255] (byte)<br/><b>H</b>: Normalized to [0–100] (hundred)</td></tr></tbody></table><p><i>Green-yellow</i> is a mixture of the colors green and yellow. It is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Web_color" title="Web color">web color</a>. It is a light <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tint" title="Tint">tint</a> of <a href="/wiki/Chartreuse_(color)" title="Chartreuse (color)">chartreuse</a>.
</p><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yellow_Crayon.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1932" data-file-width="2576" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Yellow_Crayon.JPG/220px-Yellow_Crayon.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Yellow_Crayon.JPG/330px-Yellow_Crayon.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Yellow_Crayon.JPG/440px-Yellow_Crayon.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Yellow_Crayon.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Crayola green-yellow crayon</div></div></div>
<p>"Green-yellow" is an official Crayola crayon color which was formulated in 1958.
</p><p>Green-yellow is near the center of the light <a href="/wiki/Spectrum" title="Spectrum">spectrum</a> visible to the human eye, and is very eye-catching. For this reason many emergency vehicles and uniforms exhibit green-yellow.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Harlequin">Harlequin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shades_of_green&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Harlequin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold">Harlequin</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height:12px; background-color:#3FFF00; border: 0.1px solid #000000">
 </td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><span style="position: relative; float: right; font-size: 70%"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Color/Normalized_Color_Coordinates" title="About these coordinates"><img alt="About these coordinates" data-file-height="60" data-file-width="60" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/15px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/23px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/30px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 2x" width="15"/></a></span>     Color coordinates</th></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Web_colors#Hex_triplet" title="Web colors">Hex triplet</a></th><td>
#3FFF00</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SRGB_color_space" title="SRGB color space">sRGB</a><sup><b>B</b></sup>  (<a href="/wiki/Red" title="Red">r</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green" title="Green">g</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blue" title="Blue">b</a>)</th><td>
(63, 255, 0)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><span class="nowrap"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HSV_color_space" title="HSV color space">HSV</a>       (<a href="/wiki/Hue" title="Hue">h</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saturation_(color_theory)" title="Saturation (color theory)">s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brightness" title="Brightness">v</a>)</span></th><td>
<span class="nowrap">(105°, 100%, 100%)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Source</th><td>
Maerz and Paul<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<b>B</b>: Normalized to [0–255] (byte)<br/></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><i>Harlequin</i> is a color described as being located between green and yellow (closer to green than to yellow) on the color wheel. On color plate 17 in the 1930 book <i>A Dictionary of Color</i> (see reference below), the color <i>harlequin</i> is shown as being a highly saturated rich color at a position halfway between chartreuse and green. Thus in modern color terminology, harlequin is the color halfway between green and chartreuse green on the RGB color wheel.
</p><p>The first recorded use of <i>harlequin</i> as a color name in English was in 1923.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup>
</p><p>Harlequin is a pure spectral color at approximately 552 nanometers on the visible spectrum when plotted on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CIE_chromaticity_diagram" title="CIE chromaticity diagram">CIE chromaticity diagram</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Silver Patron <a href="/wiki/Tequila" title="Tequila">tequila</a> is sold in harlequin-colored boxes.
</p><p><i>Harlequin</i> is also an adjective used to describe something that is colored in a pattern, usually a diamond-shaped pattern,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> as in the dress traditionally associated with <a href="/wiki/Harlequin" title="Harlequin">harlequins</a>. Similarly, it can mean anything multicolored or prismatic, such as opals or other precious gems which are highly variegated in color and hue. In the early 2000s, a <a href="/wiki/ChromaFlair" title="ChromaFlair">harlequin color</a> paint was invented for automobiles that appears different colors from different <a href="/wiki/Angle_of_view" title="Angle of view">angles of view</a>.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hunter_green">Hunter green</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shades_of_green&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Hunter green">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For people named "Hunter Greene", see <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Hunter_Greene_(disambiguation)" title="Hunter Greene (disambiguation)">Hunter Greene</a>.</div>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold">Hunter green</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height:12px; background-color:#355E3B; border: 0.1px solid #000000">
 </td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><span style="position: relative; float: right; font-size: 70%"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Color/Normalized_Color_Coordinates" title="About these coordinates"><img alt="About these coordinates" data-file-height="60" data-file-width="60" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/15px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/23px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/30px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 2x" width="15"/></a></span>     Color coordinates</th></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Web_colors#Hex_triplet" title="Web colors">Hex triplet</a></th><td>
#355E3B</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SRGB_color_space" title="SRGB color space">sRGB</a><sup><b>B</b></sup>  (<a href="/wiki/Red" title="Red">r</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green" title="Green">g</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blue" title="Blue">b</a>)</th><td>
(53, 94, 59)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/CMYK_color_model" title="CMYK color model">CMYK</a><sup><b>H</b></sup>   (<a href="/wiki/Cyan" title="Cyan">c</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magenta" title="Magenta">m</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yellow" title="Yellow">y</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black" title="Black">k</a>)</span></th><td>
<span class="nowrap">(75, 0, 75, 75)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><span class="nowrap"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HSV_color_space" title="HSV color space">HSV</a>       (<a href="/wiki/Hue" title="Hue">h</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saturation_(color_theory)" title="Saturation (color theory)">s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brightness" title="Brightness">v</a>)</span></th><td>
<span class="nowrap">(120°, 45%, 45%)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Source</th><td>
<a class="external text" href="http://tx4.us/nbs/nbs-h.htm" rel="nofollow">ISCC-NBS #137</a></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<b>B</b>: Normalized to [0–255] (byte)<br/><b>H</b>: Normalized to [0–100] (hundred)</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><i>Hunter green</i> is a color that is a representation of the color worn by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hunter" title="Hunter">hunters</a> in the 19th century. Most hunters began wearing the color olive drab instead of hunter green about the beginning of the 20th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Some hunters still wear hunter green clothing or hunter green <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bandana" title="Bandana">bandanas</a>.
</p><p>The first recorded use of <i>hunter green</i> as a color name in English was in 1892.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup>
</p><p>Hunter green has been the official primary color of the <a href="/wiki/Green_Bay_Packers" title="Green Bay Packers">Green Bay Packers</a> since 1957, the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Jets" title="New York Jets">New York Jets</a> since 1998, one of the two official colors of <a href="/wiki/Ohio_University" title="Ohio University">Ohio University</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oswego_State" title="Oswego State">Oswego State</a>, and one of the two official colors of the <a href="/wiki/Phi_Kappa_Psi" title="Phi Kappa Psi">Phi Kappa Psi</a> fraternity.
</p><p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bandana_code" title="Bandana code">bandana code</a> of the gay leather subculture, a hunter green bandana, if worn on the left, indicates that one is a <i>leather daddy</i>, whereas if a hunter green bandana is worn on the right, it indicates that one is looking for a <i>leather daddy</i>, i.e., looking for a <i>daddy-boy</i> relationship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Andrews_2010_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-Andrews_2010-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hankycode_on_gaycitiusa.com_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hankycode_on_gaycitiusa.com-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hankycode_on_leathernjonline.com_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hankycode_on_leathernjonline.com-69">[69]</a></sup> The color displayed at upper right matches the color that is used in the bandana code.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Prison_uniform" title="Prison uniform">Prison uniforms</a> issued by the <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Department_of_Corrections_and_Community_Supervision" title="New York State Department of Corrections and Community Supervision">New York State Department of Corrections and Community Supervision</a> are colored hunter green.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<p><i>India green</i>, the color of the lower band of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_National_Flag" title="Indian National Flag">Indian National Flag</a>, represents fertility and prosperity.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Islamic_green">Islamic green</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shades_of_green&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Islamic green">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold">Islamic green</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height:12px; background-color:#009000; border: 0.1px solid #000000">

<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Green_in_Islam" title="Green in Islam">Green in Islam</a></div>
<p><i>Islamic green</i> is the shade of green used in the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Flag of the Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Flag of the Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a>.
</p><p>Green symbolizes <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> because the tribe of the prophet <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a> had a green banner and because green represented paradise to desert dwelling bedouin tribes when they gathered at an oasis. 
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jade">Jade</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shades_of_green&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Jade">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold">Jade</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height:12px; background-color:#00A86B; border: 0.1px solid #000000">
 </td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><span style="position: relative; float: right; font-size: 70%"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Color/Normalized_Color_Coordinates" title="About these coordinates"><img alt="About these coordinates" data-file-height="60" data-file-width="60" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/15px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/23px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/30px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 2x" width="15"/></a></span>     Color coordinates</th></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Web_colors#Hex_triplet" title="Web colors">Hex triplet</a></th><td>

<b>B</b>: Normalized to [0–255] (byte)<br/></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><i>Jade</i>, also called <i>jade green</i>, is a representation of the color of the <a href="/wiki/Gemstone" title="Gemstone">gemstone</a> called <a href="/wiki/Jade" title="Jade">jade</a>, although the stone itself varies widely in hue.
</p><p>The color name <i>jade green</i> was first used in Spanish in the form <i>piedra de ijada</i> in 1569.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jadestein.jpg"><img alt="A slab of jade" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="536" data-file-width="438" height="269" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Jadestein.jpg/220px-Jadestein.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Jadestein.jpg/330px-Jadestein.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/00/Jadestein.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jadestein.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A slab of <a href="/wiki/Jade" title="Jade">jade</a></div></div></div>
<p>The first recorded use of <i>jade green</i> as a color name in English was in 1892.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kelly_green">Kelly green</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shades_of_green&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Kelly green">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><span id="Kelly_green"></span>
</p>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold">Kelly green</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height:12px; background-color:#4CBB17; border: 0.1px solid #000000">
 </td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><span style="position: relative; float: right; font-size: 70%"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Color/Normalized_Color_Coordinates" title="About these coordinates"><img alt="About these coordinates" data-file-height="60" data-file-width="60" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/15px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/23px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/30px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 2x" width="15"/></a></span>     Color coordinates</th></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Web_colors#Hex_triplet" title="Web colors">Hex triplet</a></th><td>

<span class="nowrap">(101°, 87%, 73%)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Source</th><td>

<b>B</b>: Normalized to [0–255] (byte)<br/><b>H</b>: Normalized to [0–100] (hundred)</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><i>Kelly green</i> is an American term. The name derives from the fact that the surname <i>Kelly</i>, as well as the color green, are both popular in Ireland. The use of the term as a color name occurred at least as far back as 1917.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Malachite">Malachite</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shades_of_green&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Malachite">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold">Malachite</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height:12px; background-color:#0BDA51; border: 0.1px solid #000000">
 </td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><span style="position: relative; float: right; font-size: 70%"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Color/Normalized_Color_Coordinates" title="About these coordinates"><img alt="About these coordinates" data-file-height="60" data-file-width="60" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/15px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/23px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Gtk-dialog-info.svg/30px-Gtk-dialog-info.svg.png 2x" width="15"/></a></span>     Color coordinates</th></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Web_colors#Hex_triplet" title="Web colors">Hex triplet</a></th><td>

(11, 218, 81)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/CMYK_color_model" title="CMYK color model">CMYK</a><sup><b>H</b></sup>   (<a href="/wiki/Cyan" title="Cyan">c</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magenta" title="Magenta">m</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yellow" title="Yellow">y</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black" title="Black">k</a>)</span></th><td>
<span class="nowrap">(60, 0, 40, 22)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><span class="nowrap"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HSV_color_space" title="HSV color space">HSV</a>       (<a href="/wiki/Hue" title="Hue">h</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saturation_(color_theory)" title="Saturation (color theory)">s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brightness" title="Brightness">v</a>)</span></th><td>
<span class="nowrap">(140°, 95%, 85%)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Source</th><td>
Maerz and Paul<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<b>B</b>: Normalized to [0–255] (byte)<br/><b>H</b>: Normalized to [0–100] (hundred)</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><i>Malachite</i>, also called <i>malachite green</i>, is a color that is a representation of the color of the mineral <a href="/wiki/Malachite" title="Malachite">malachite</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Malachite_polie_(R%C3%A9publique_d%C3%A9mocratique_du_Congo).JPG"><img alt="Polished malachite" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="3898" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Malachite_polie_%28R%C3%A9publique_d%C3%A9mocratique_du_Congo%29.JPG/220px-Malachite_polie_%28R%C3%A9publique_d%C3%A9mocratique_du_Congo%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Malachite_polie_%28R%C3%A9publique_d%C3%A9mocratique_du_Congo%29.JPG/330px-Malachite_polie_%28R%C3%A9publique_d%C3%A9mocratique_du_Congo%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Malachite_polie_%28R%C3%A9publique_d%C3%A9mocratique_du_Congo%29.JPG/440px-Malachite_polie_%28R%C3%A9publique_d%C3%A9mocratique_du_Congo%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Malachite_polie_(R%C3%A9publique_d%C3%A9mocratique_du_Congo).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Polished <a href="/wiki/Malachite" title="Malachite">malachite</a></div></div></div>
<p>The first recorded use of <i>malachite green</i> as a color name in English was in the 1200s (exact year uncertain).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
